ARIE 1927-1928 [ARIE 050]

Viswanatha, S. V., ed. 1929. Annual Report on South-Indian Epigraphy for the Year Ending 31st March 1928. Calcutta: Government of India.



[APPENDIX] A. List of copper-plates examined during the year 1927-28.



ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/1 (page )
Place
The Raja Saheb of Sandur, through the Political Agent.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Kṛishṇarāyadēva
Date
Śaka 1210 (wrong), Sarvadhāri, Vaiśākha, śu. 13, Monday.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
The writing looks quite modern. Purports to be a record executed during the reign of the Pradhānapaṇḍita Sāḷava Apaji-Panta in the presence of the assembly of several persons, making a gift of land to a carpenter named Rāmōju, son of Dēvōju. The grant is evidently a forgery.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/2 (page )
Place
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1740, Bahudhānya.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inserittions.
Remarks
Registers the confirmation of the boundaries of Sāṇḍūru-jahāgīru by Thomas Munro Baha-dūr, made in the time of Śiva-Rao Hindu-Rao Ghōrpaḍe.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/3 (page )
Place
The Trustee of the Śri-Mūkām-bikā temple at Kollūru, Coondapoor taluk, South Kanara district.
Dynasty
Keḷadi
King
Vīrabhadra-Nāyaka
Date
Śaka 1565, Sva-bhānu, Kārttika, śu. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inserittions.
Remarks
Registers a grant of the income of two villages named Koḷambaḷike-Rāḍigrāma in Kabu-nāḍa-sīme and Vaḷarūra-[va]ṭa in Niru-ḷanāḍa-sīme by the king, for worship, offerings and lamps to the goddess Mūkām-bikā and the subsidiary deities in the temple at Kollūru.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/4 (page )
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Śaka 1565, Chitrabhānu, Phālguṇa, śu. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inserittions.
Remarks
Records the remission of taxes on some lands in Hose-ūru by the king in favour of the temple of Mūkāmbikā-Amma at Kollūru for its requirements, in return for a lump sum of 200 varāhas received from a certain Śāntayya.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/5 (page )
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Veṅkaṭappa-Nāyaka
Date
Śaka 1550, Prabhava, Āshāḍha, śu. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inserittions.
Remarks
Records the allotment of the village Kaḷasi in Jālida-sīme by the king to a certain Chik-kaṁna, for a lump sum of 330 varāhas, for the maintenance out of its annual income in paddy, of a feeding choultry established by the donor in a suburb of Dharmapuri in Haṁnarada-sīme. The management was vested in the temple of Mūkāmbikā.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/6 (page )
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrabhadra-Nāyaka
Date
Śaka 1564 Vṛisha, Vaiśākha, śu. 10.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inserittions.
Remarks
Registers the allotment of the annual income from certain specified sources in a few villages amounting to 1,002 varāhas and the income in kind from 9 other villages by the king, for the maintenance of the daily worship and offerings in the temple of Mūkāmbikā at Kollūru.

South-Indian Inserittions.

Seems to be an incorrect copy of the above record, but left incomplete.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/7 (page 6)
Place
P.Ayyasvami Gurukkal, Anaimalai, Pollachi taluk, Coimbatore district.
Dynasty
Mysore
King
Kṛishṇarāja-Voḍeya, ‘ruling from Śrīraṅgapaṭṭaṇa’.
Date
Śaka 1685, Kali 4864, Svabhānu, Phālguṇa, śu. 2, Sun-day, Uttarā-bhādra, Śubhayōga, Bālavākara-ṇa.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Records the establishment by Mādyaya, the headman of Kōyammuttūru, of an agrahāra called Mādhavapura to the west of Ānemale, and the allotment of shares of land to several Brahmans residing therein.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/8 (page 6)
Place
A resident of Milatti, Kalyan-drug taluk, Anantapur district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1658, Nala, Kārt-tika, śu. 15, Sunday.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Origin
Do.
Edition
Do.
Remarks
Registers the sale of the karaṇikam-right together with 3 villages, Varle, Puli-Timmāreḍḍipalle and Kāparlapalle by Subayya (Subbayya) and Apakeṇḍaya in a partition between themselves, to a certain Veṅkaṭagiriyappa, in return for 250 varāhas which they had borrowed from him.
ARIE/1927-1928/A/1927-28/9 (page 6)
Place
Mr. M.Somasekhara Sarma of the ‘Bhārati’ Office, Madras.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga.
King
Dēvēndravarman
Date
Śaka 1103
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit in Nāgarī
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Written in very faulty Sanskrit. Records the grant of the village Rēviṇiji in Pañcha-vishaya to Nārāyaṇa, son of Rēvaṇa-Nāyaka and to Aitama-Śōmayā[ji], by Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Rāṇaka Śrī-Dharma-Khēḍi, son of Śrī-Bhīma-Khēḍi, who is described as a Paramamāhēśvara and Pañ-chavishayādhipati, and who belonged to the Kadamba family. (Published by Mr. Sarma in the Bhārati, Vol. VII.)

KURNOOL DISTRICT



NANDIKOTKUR TALUK



ARIE/1927-1928/B/1927-28/9 (page 7)
Place
Sivapuram.—On a stone plant-ed in front of the Mallēśvara temple.
Dynasty
Western Chāḷukya.
King
Bhuvanaikamalladēva
Date
Śaka 991, Saumya, Āshāḍha, .. Tuesday, solar eclipse.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers a grant of land by the king at the request of his queens Rēvaladēvī and Mailaladēvī to Surēśvara-Paṇḍita, the disciple of Gaṅgarāśi-Bhaṭṭāraka, the āchārya of the Mosaṅgi Brahmēśvara temple, who is referred to as a follower of the Kāḷāmukha-samaya and gets a number of attributes of that creed.
ARIE/1927-1928/B/1927-28/10 (page 7)
Place
On another stone planted in the same temple.
Dynasty
…
King
…

Chāḷukya-Vikrama year 33, Sarva-[dhāri], Phālgu-ṇa, śu. 5, Vaḍḍa-vāra.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers a grant of land by Ārya-Paṇḍitadēva of Śivapura to two individuals for the renovation of the temple of Brahmēśvara. Mentions Mailaladēvī.
ARIE/1927-1928/B/1927-28/11 (page 8)
Place
On the same stone
Dynasty
Western Chālukya.
King
Trailōkyamalladēva
Date
Śaka[98]0, Viḷam-bi, Vaiśākha, paurṇami, Mon-day, Vyatīpāta.

Kannaḍa

Registers the grant of some lands in the village Śivapura in Kanne-nāḍu to god Ādibhairava of the western gate of the temple of Mallikārjuna, by queen Mailaladēvi and Ballavarasa, for the maintenance of a sattra for the ascetics visiting the temple.

ARIE/1927-1928/B/1927-28/13 (page 8)
Place
Bhairasamudram.—On a slab planted in front of the temple.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara.
King
Kṛishṇarāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1444, Chitra-bhānu, Pushya, śu. 10, Sunday, Makara-Saṅk-rānti.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village Bhairasamudram in Kugari-nāḍu, a subdivision of Kunduripi-sīma, as sarva-mānya for worship and offerings in the temple of Tiru-vēṅgaḷanātha of Vēmpalapariti by Kundurpi Narasa-Nāyaniṁgāru, who had the titles ‘Mahānāyaṁkāchārya, Bhāshadappuva-nāyaṁkara-gaṁḍa’ and ‘Marihokkare-kāva’, for the merit of his father Kundiripi Timma-Nāya-niṁgāru and Rāyasam Koṇḍamarasayya. The shares allotted to the sthānikas and the archakas of the temple are given at the end.

Registers that the people of Raṅgasamudram, the Gauḍas, Sēnabōgas and the Ayagārs and the Pārapatya Timmap-paya, the agent of Timmaṇa-Nāyaka, constructed a temple of Basaliṅgadēva, and granted some land in the village for the maintenance of worship and offerings to the deity.

DHARWAR DISTRICT



RON TALUK



ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/1 (page 20)
Place

Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Koṭṭigadēva
Date
Śaka 891, Pramō-[dūta], Phālguṇa, ba.., Friday.

Remarks
Damaged. Refers to the construction of a maṇḍapa and a temple. Registers a gift of land and gold to the temple by Chellayya. Verses in praise of Gaṟduga-Rayya of Beṅgi. The inscription was composed by the poet Nāraṇa.

Place
In the same place
Dynasty
Western Chāḷukya.
King
Tribhuvanamalladēva
Date
Chāḷukya-Vikrama year 7, Dundubhi, Phālguṇa, ba. 5, Monday.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers the grant of a land to the temple of Mūlasthānadēva by Gaṅgara-Bāchimayya after washing the feet of Chan-drabhūshaṇa-Paṇḍitadēva, the āchārya of the temple. The gift was made for worship, decoration, etc., of the god, the feeding of the ascetics and the renovation of the temple, when Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Bhūlōkamalla-Permāḍi was governing Kisukāḍu-70, Bāgaḍage-70 and Nareyaṁgal-12.

Śaka 1091, Virōdhi, Pushya, śu. 5, Thursday, Uttarāyaṇa-saṁ-kramaṇa.

Kannaḍa
Remarks

Western Chāḷukya.
King
Pratāpa Chakravartin Trailōkyamalla-dēva.
Date
7th year, Dhātu, Mārgaśira, śu. 13, Monday, Vyatī-pāta, Uttarāyaṇa-saṁkramaṇa.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Mentions a certain Daṇḍanāyaka Duggimayya who made a gift of land after purchasing it from a certain Gāmuṇḍa. Registers grants of land made by Jōga-Gāmuṇḍa and other local men to the tank called Vi[di]geyakeṟe. Also states that carpenters, blacksmiths, etc., offered their free services to the tank.

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa

Mentions the engraver Taila.

BAGALKOT TALUK



ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/239 (page 33)
Place
Havēli.—On a slab set up in front of the Māruti temple.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1744
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Kannaḍa in Nāgarī
Remarks
Records that Appūrāya, who was the Subhēdāra (Subedar) of Bāgaḍikōṭi under the Kuṁpaṇi-Sarakāra (East India Company), renovated the village Havēli otherwise known as Gōpālapura, constructed there a temple of Hanumān and a well, and made endowments for worship and offerings in the temple.
ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/240 (page 33)
Place
Honnakatti.—On three pieces of a broken slab kept in the Māruti temple.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1750, Sarva-dhāri.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa in Nāgarī
Remarks
States that a certain Gōpālappa, grandson of Vaḍavāḍigi-Rāyappa, re-inhabited the village Honnāyakanakaṭi which had been deserted for a long time, and constructed there a temple and a well. Mentions Kuṁpaṇi-Sarakāra.

ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/264 (page 34)
Place
Mankani.—On a slab in the Śiva temple called the Dēgula.
Dynasty
Yādava
King
Siṁhaṇadēva, ruling from Dēvagiri
Date
Śaka 1128, Krōdhana, Amāvāse, Monday, solar eclipse.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Damaged. Records that Kēśavadēva, the brother of Sahadēva-Daṇḍanātha who was the governor of Tardevaḍi—1,000 and who belonged to Vāchhasya-gōtra and Sahavāsa-kula, built a temple at Maṅkaṇi situated in Tardevāḍi country and installed in it the gods Lakshmīnṛisiṁha, Sādēvēśvara and Vāsudēva. Registers a gift of land for worship and offerings to these gods.

ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/267 (page 34)
Place
Kop.—On a slab lying behind the temple of Durgavva.
Dynasty
Western Chāḷukya.
King
Bhuvanaikamalladēva
Date
Śaka 997, Rākshasa, Vai-śākha, śu. 3, Monday.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village Bādubbepāḷu situated in Kisukāḍu-70, for worship and offerings in the temple of Svayambhu-Nagarēśvara of Vikramapura and for the maintenance of the students in the maṭha attached to the temple, by Ballavarasa, at the request of Nimba-Daṇḍa-nātha, while the king was encamped at Taṅgoḍage situated on the north bank of Perddoṟe in Kārakuṟuva-40 which was included in Tarddavāḍi. The grant was made after washing the feet of Tatpurusha-Paṇḍita, disciple of Tribhuvanaśakti-Paṇḍita of the Kāḷāmukha sect. Also registers another gift by Chandarasa of Orkkunda for worship and offerings to the god Svayaṁbhu-Kalidēva.

BADAMI TALUK



ARIE/1927-1928/E/1927-28/272 (page 35)
*)Nos. 272 to 289 were copied in 1925. Two Marāṭhi inscriptions at Sholapur fort were also copied along with these. One of them belongs to the reign of Sulatāna Mahāmada Adalśāha Pādaśāha and is dated in Śaka 1575, Vijaya, Āśvija, ba. 5, Saturday, and the other which is dated in Śaka 1466, Krōdhi, Āshāḍha does not refer itself to the reign of any king.
